  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dd334fd5-2357-4a4e-a369-a645eb5d4999'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText10698810886297320769" style="display:none"><b>The chilling psychological thriller from the #1 bestselling author of <i>I Am Watching You</i>.</b><br /><br />On a train with her husband, miles from home and their four-year-old son, Ben, Sophie receives a chilling phone call. Two boys are in hospital after a tragic accident. One of them is Ben.<br /><br />She thought she could trust Emma, her new friend, to look after her little boy. After all, Emma’s a kindred spirit—someone Sophie was sure she could bare her soul to, despite the village rumours. But Sophie can’t shake the feeling that she’s made an unforgivable mistake and now her whole family is in danger.<br /><br />Because how well does she know Emma, really? Should she have trusted her at all?<br /><br />Time is running out. Powerless to help her child, still hours from home, Sophie is about to discover the truth. And her life will never be the same.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666960969" />
    <a title="Joey R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r"><img alt="Joey R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528158785p2/11232712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666960969?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey R." href="/user/show/11232712-joey-r">Joey R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666960969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10309082812692133163">2.0 Stars— After being floored with how good the first thriller I read from Teresa Driscoll (“I Am Watching You”) was, I was not as impressed with “The Friend”. In my opinion, “The Friend” took a very long time for anything (and I do mean anything) to happen, and when it did, it was very slow developing. 90% of the novel is the main character, Sophie, telling her story of meeting and becoming friends with the new woman in town, Emma. Emma appears to Sophie to be a perfect new friend , but some o</span>
  <span id="freeText10309082812692133163" style="display:none">2.0 Stars— After being floored with how good the first thriller I read from Teresa Driscoll (“I Am Watching You”) was, I was not as impressed with “The Friend”. In my opinion, “The Friend” took a very long time for anything (and I do mean anything) to happen, and when it did, it was very slow developing. 90% of the novel is the main character, Sophie, telling her story of meeting and becoming friends with the new woman in town, Emma. Emma appears to Sophie to be a perfect new friend , but some of the people in Sophie’s circle of friends and family don’t like her. As the story progresses, the author reveals more and more about Emma until a major crisis takes place for which Emma gets the blame. This is the turning point of the novel, but despite being well written, the snail’s pace makes this one hard to read and enjoy. The conclusion is also a let down as I expected a lot more diabolical plot twists and a lot less information about the two ladies opening a deli. Avoid this one unless you like very slow building plots with little reward in the end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10309082812692133163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2293722077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2293722077" />
    <a title="Jules" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4824134-jules"><img alt="Jules" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561752629p2/4824134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2293722077?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jules" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jules" href="/user/show/4824134-jules">Jules</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35920727-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2293722077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10699303240170528378">Having loved <i>I Am Watching You</i>, I was really looking forward to <i>The Friend</i>. I’m pleased to say that I absolutely LOVED it.<br/><br/><i>The Friend</i> had me gripped and intrigued throughout, as I wasn’t sure where the story was going, so eagerly needed to read more to find out. This thought provoking psychological thriller was full of mystery, intrigue, suspense and an impressively manipulative character. Ooh, I do love a good sociopath to keep me on my toes!<br/><br/>I really don’t want to go into detail about the plot, </span>
  <span id="freeText10699303240170528378" style="display:none">Having loved <i>I Am Watching You</i>, I was really looking forward to <i>The Friend</i>. I’m pleased to say that I absolutely LOVED it.<br /><br /><i>The Friend</i> had me gripped and intrigued throughout, as I wasn’t sure where the story was going, so eagerly needed to read more to find out. This thought provoking psychological thriller was full of mystery, intrigue, suspense and an impressively manipulative character. Ooh, I do love a good sociopath to keep me on my toes!<br /><br />I really don’t want to go into detail about the plot, because with many psychological thrillers I think it’s best to go in blind, so if you like the sound of the blurb, please give this a go. I just have to say that I was loving this story so much, I enjoyed being in the moment and never consciously tried to work out where the story was going or how it was going to end, so everything came as a surprise to me.<br /><br />Teresa Driscoll is very good at creating well developed and believable characters that I often find easy to connect with. However, in her thrillers, rather than her women’s fiction books (which are also wonderful, so do check those out too), I find myself feeling much more suspicious of the characters. Unsure of what will happen and which characters to fully trust. <br /><br /><i>“Not every hour is equal. Ask an insomniac how long the night is”</i> - I relate to this far more than I’d like to. As someone who has had severe insomnia for many years. I’d like to clarify that nights are exceptionally long, yet at the same time nowhere near long enough. I need more sleep!<br /><br /><i>“To know the Lizard is to drive past the flat and unpromising landscape of the RNAS base, smiling inwardly at the trick of it. For, just a few miles in any of several directions from the neatly fenced but unlovely facility, there is this feast of the unexpected and unspoilt.”</i> – It’s true, going past the military base then approaching the Lizard is so magical. The Lizard landscape is like a hidden treasure. I doubt I’ll ever become fully used to the magic of it. On another note, the power behind that neat fence steals my husband and controls my life. I sometimes feel like a character in a dystopian novel. Give me back my freedom!<br /><br />I loved this whole book and the epilogue too. I highly recommend this book to fans of psychological thrillers. I actually think I enjoyed <i>The Friend</i> even more than <i>I Am Watching You</i>. They are both standalone novels. Needless to say, this is yet another brilliant 5 star read from this talented author. I can’t wait to see what she comes up with next.<br /><br /><b><i>The Friend</i> is available to pre-order on Amazon:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B074CH1CDH/">https://www.amazon.co.uk/gp/product/B...</a><br /><br /><b>My review is also available on my blog here:</b><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://littlemissnosleep.wordpress.com/2018/03/07/bookreview-5-stars-the-friend-by-teresa-driscoll-teresadriscoll-publicityshona-agentmilburn-thefriend-psychological-thriller-mystery-fiction-book-review/">https://littlemissnosleep.wordpress.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10699303240170528378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2265863739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7105739056059492864">EXCERPT: I had seen the worst of what two people can do to each other. My neighbours and friends. How could I be all right?<br/><br/>I had walked into a room, happy and relaxed, with my son waiting for me on the doorstep. <br/><br/>Unknowing. Innocent. Me. Sophie. The woman who allegedly had this chocolate box life. <br/><br/>I had walked in smiling and been met with a scene which I never, ever want anyone to imagine. <br/><br/>Not my son. Not my husband. Not even the police Inspector with the wrong notebook and all the wrong ideas ab</span>
  <span id="freeText7105739056059492864" style="display:none">EXCERPT: I had seen the worst of what two people can do to each other. My neighbours and friends. How could I be all right?<br /><br />I had walked into a room, happy and relaxed, with my son waiting for me on the doorstep. <br /><br />Unknowing. Innocent. Me. Sophie. The woman who allegedly had this chocolate box life. <br /><br />I had walked in smiling and been met with a scene which I never, ever want anyone to imagine. <br /><br />Not my son. Not my husband. Not even the police Inspector with the wrong notebook and all the wrong ideas about all of us. <br /><br />It was unreal. That is what it was. Shocking and unreal. <br /><br />ABOUT THIS BOOK: On a train with her husband, miles from home and their four-year-old son, Ben, Sophie receives a chilling phone call. Two boys are in hospital after a tragic accident. One of them is Ben.<br /><br />She thought she could trust Emma, her new friend, to look after her little boy. After all, Emma’s a kindred spirit—someone Sophie was sure she could bare her soul to, despite the village rumours. But Sophie can’t shake the feeling that she’s made an unforgivable mistake and now her whole family is in danger.<br /><br />Because how well does she know Emma, really? Should she have trusted her at all?<br /><br />Time is running out. Powerless to help her child, still hours from home, Sophie is about to discover the truth. And her life will never be the same.<br /><br />MY THOUGHTS: Now that I am breathing normally again, am I going to be able to write a review that does The Friend by Teresa Driscoll justice? I read this book overnight, unable to put it down, consumed by the need to know what happens. <br /><br />It starts off light-heartedly, two women with children of a similar age meeting over a crashed furniture truck and a burst bag of parsnips. Well, it could happen to anyone. Great friendships have been struck in stranger situations. But this friendship quickly spirals into a series of dramatic, suspenseful occurrences where you are never quite sure who is reliable, and who is playing games. Manipulative games. Dangerous games that had me forgetting to breathe. <br /><br />The final few chapters had me crying like a baby. Teresa Driscoll had me running through the whole gamut of my emotions. I have not read her previous psychological thriller, I am Watching You, but I intend remedying that. Soon. There is not one word that I would change in this superb read. <br /><br />And after reading The Friend, I will be seriously questioning my own judgement next time I feel an instant affinity with someone. <br /><br />Thank you to Thomas and Mercer via Netgalley for providing a digital copy of The Friend by Teresa Driscoll for review. All opinions expressed in this review are entirely my own personal opinions. <br /><br />Please refer to my Goodreads.com profile page or the 'about' page on sandysbookaday.wordpress.com for an explanation of my rating system. <br /><br />This review and others are also published on my blog sandysbookaday.wordpress.com <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/2018/03/26/the-friend-by-teresa-driscoll/">https://sandysbookaday.wordpress.com/...</a></span>

  <span id="freeText12538688803813596471" style="display:none">The book begins with Sophie on a train ride, hours from home, when she receives a devastating phone call that her 4 year old son has been rushed to the hospital and in need of surgery. Sophie left Ben with her good friend Emma and her son Theo for just one night. How did this happen? <br /><br />We flashback to the beginning of Emma and Sophie's friendship.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Li&#39;l Owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Li&#39;l Owl" href="/user/show/48372551-li-l-owl"> Li&#39;l Owl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781542046664" href="/book/show/35906811-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=owl-s-kindle-own">owl-s-kindle-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=uk-author-setting">uk-author-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=detective-police-procedural-sheriff">detective-police-procedural-sheriff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=mystery-crime-suspense-thriller">mystery-crime-suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=owl-s-audible-audiobooks-own">owl-s-audible-audiobooks-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=psychological-suspense-thriller">psychological-suspense-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2375519935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7191900458006075186"><b>Compelling and dramatic! A mother's worst nightmare!</b><br/><br/>Sophie thought she could trust Emma to care for Theo and Ben and to keep them safe. <br/>She was wrong.<br/><br/><i>'The boys... There's been some kind of accident, Sophie.'<br/><br/>More than two hundred miles away, my child is in a hospital bed being cared for by strangers.</i><br/><br/>Sophie and Mark Hill and their four year old son, Ben, have moved to a small village in Devon. Mark must still commute to London until he can relocate his business closer to Devin. <br/><br/>Why Devon? <br/><i>'I'll fe</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7191900458006075186" style="display:none"><b>Compelling and dramatic! A mother's worst nightmare!</b><br /><br />Sophie thought she could trust Emma to care for Theo and Ben and to keep them safe. <br />She was wrong.<br /><br /><i>'The boys... There's been some kind of accident, Sophie.'<br /><br />More than two hundred miles away, my child is in a hospital bed being cared for by strangers.</i><br /><br />Sophie and Mark Hill and their four year old son, Ben, have moved to a small village in Devon. Mark must still commute to London until he can relocate his business closer to Devin. <br /><br />Why Devon? <br /><i>'I'll feel safer in the country, Mark. A different person. More cooking. Less stressing. It's what the baby needs. What we all need.'<br /><br />The worst irony? I moved us to the country because I thought it would be safer.</i><br /><br />Emma Carter and her four year old son, Theo move to Tedbury shortly after the Hill family. Ben and Theo become fast friends, Sophie and Emma follow suit. <br /><br /><i>We met on a Thursday. Two boys. Two mothers. Much later, and especially on that train, I will torture myself for the curiosity and excitement I felt; the enthusiasm with which I so easily opened my door to it all. </i><br /><br />When Mark meets Emma at a dinner party it seems that he doesn't feel the same way. <br /><br /><i>'You didn't like her, did you?' <br />I turned to monitor his reaction. He shrugged. His eyes said I was right. </i><br /><br />Then Sophie's good friend, Helen, comes for a visit and it's clear that she isn't too keen on Emma, either. <br /><i>It was the first time Helen had ever annoyed me. She had so clearly failed to take to Emma that I even wondered if, like everyone else, she was a bit jealous.... </i><br /><br />****<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35906836.The_Friend" title="The Friend by Teresa Driscoll" rel="nofollow noopener">The Friend</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7970305.Teresa_Driscoll" title="Teresa Driscoll" rel="nofollow noopener">Teresa Driscoll</a> is written with strong characters, a dynamic storyline, and a fast pace that kept me turning the pages. In a small village rumors flow like water, creating more questions than answers. The teaser drew me in and propelled me forward all the way to the startling conclusion. Of course, I <i>had</i> to know what had happened to Ben and Theo! Once I started I didn't want to stop until I found out!</span>

Continuing the analogy, one can still argue whether enough twists and turns were taken to make the ride an enjoyable mystery.<br/><br/>Do the ends really justify the means in this case? I think not.   <span id="freeText3363913348497328499" style="display:none">"The Friend" by Teresa Driscoll is like driving a car in the first or second gear for around 80 percent of the journey, and then pushing the throttle all the way in for the last mile. Continuing the analogy, one can still argue whether enough twists and turns were taken to make the ride an enjoyable mystery.<br /><br />Do the ends really justify the means in this case? I think not. After sitting along for the plot to take its own sweet time to develop, I was getting ready to tighten my seat-belt in anticipation of quick turns, which came, but not in adequate numbers as to fulfill my expectations.<br /><br /><b><u>Interesting quotes</u>:</b><br />On how an insomniac measures time<br /><i>"Not every hour is equal. Ask an insomniac how long the night is."</i><br /><br />On time and human nature<br /><i>"Some people you can know for years and yet not at all."</i><br /><br />On things we are capable of doing for love<br /><i>"the biggest shock and most important lesson was realising what other people are truly capable of. But – turns out there is a much greater and more chilling shock. Learning – in the face of evil and in the name of love – what you are capable of yourself."</i><br /><br /></span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146684969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7315378019921863499">As in Teresa Driscoll’s first psychological thriller, ( I am Watching You) we begin this journey on a train...<br/><br/>On this train we meet Sophie. She is miles away from home when she gets the call that her son Ben has been in a serious accident while under the care of her new friend Emma. <br/><br/>A woman she bonded with immediately when Emma moved into her old friend Caroline’s house, with her young son Theo, in tow. <br/><br/>A woman that nobody else seems to like or trust. <br/><br/>Told in alternating chapters of “Today” and </span>
  <span id="freeText7315378019921863499" style="display:none">As in Teresa Driscoll’s first psychological thriller, ( I am Watching You) we begin this journey on a train...<br /><br />On this train we meet Sophie. She is miles away from home when she gets the call that her son Ben has been in a serious accident while under the care of her new friend Emma. <br /><br />A woman she bonded with immediately when Emma moved into her old friend Caroline’s house, with her young son Theo, in tow. <br /><br />A woman that nobody else seems to like or trust. <br /><br />Told in alternating chapters of “Today” and “Before”...<br /><br />The suspense builds steadily in the “Before” chapters, as you wonder who Emma really is, and why she moved to town. <br /><br />The tension builds a bit more slowly in the “Today” chapters, as Sophie struggles to get any information about Ben’s condition, and cannot get to the hospital fast enough. <br /><br />If you love psychological "suspense "novels with a few surprises that don’t require you to completely suspend disbelief, then give this author a try! <br /><br />4.5 stars <br /><br /><br />She is two for two in the psychological thriller genre for me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7315378019921863499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512625622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3749930179736809859">I usually ask others to read books from different countries and origins. But my own practice lacks that determination. I would try to avoid foreign authors may be due to my comfort zone with Indian authors. Not just that once in a while when I take books of the said category my mind went through a hell lot of tantrums. It makes me feel "I am not getting it Vishnu. Don't read more". But then my heart pursue it till my mind able to cope up with narration style. "The Friend" by Teresa Driscoll was </span>
  <span id="freeText3749930179736809859" style="display:none">I usually ask others to read books from different countries and origins. But my own practice lacks that determination. I would try to avoid foreign authors may be due to my comfort zone with Indian authors. Not just that once in a while when I take books of the said category my mind went through a hell lot of tantrums. It makes me feel "I am not getting it Vishnu. Don't read more". But then my heart pursue it till my mind able to cope up with narration style. "The Friend" by Teresa Driscoll was one such experience for me. Until I reached the milestone of 70 pages my mind has tried all possible distraction to leave the book but I persisted.<br /><br />The friend is the story of a countryside town called Tedbury. The protagonist of our story is Sophie. The author has divided suspense into two parallels. In current time Sophie got a call that her son along with another kid was admitted to the hospital. She was on the train when she received the news. During the long train journey, she recalled how she ended up in this situation. So what she recalled? There comes our mysterious character called Emma. A new lady in Tedbury who became Sophie's best friend from the day one. The lady whom disliked by his husband and closed friends but she didn't listen to. It is her (Emma's) past that is bothering current of Sophies's life. A suspense that makes you go through the book.<br /><br />Coming to writing style, it is a completely different experience for me. I am not kidding when I said I struggle to overcome the benchmark of 70 pages. the book is intermingled with past-present, character-emotion, story-fillers. The books not for beginners. You need to read it with full concentration. Coming to language portion, it is easy to follow. Characterization is brilliant and plots it also excellent. Only weak nerve it the narration style, if you can catch it you will love the book. I fumble for the first 3rd and that has affected my experience overall.<br /><br /><br />Detailed Review Link - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://chevusread.blogspot.com/2018/09/book-review-friend-by-teresa-driscoll.html">http://chevusread.blogspot.com/2018/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3749930179736809859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2267896378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2267896378" />
    <a title="Nicki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8862640-nicki"><img alt="Nicki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538936970p2/8862640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2267896378?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicki" href="/user/show/8862640-nicki">Nicki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2267896378" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10605164503104914647">Sophie has suddenly found herself trapped in every loving parents worst nightmare.She is on a train,hours from.home and has just received a chilling phone call.Her four year old son Ben and his young friend are in hospital after a serious accident.<br/><br/>Sophie is at her wits end,she thought Ben would be safe with her best friend Emma.Someone Sophie had bared her soul to,despite the village rumours.But now Sophie is beginning to wonder if she has made a unforgivable mistake.<br/><br/>Because how well does she kn</span>
  <span id="freeText10605164503104914647" style="display:none">Sophie has suddenly found herself trapped in every loving parents worst nightmare.She is on a train,hours from.home and has just received a chilling phone call.Her four year old son Ben and his young friend are in hospital after a serious accident.<br /><br />Sophie is at her wits end,she thought Ben would be safe with her best friend Emma.Someone Sophie had bared her soul to,despite the village rumours.But now Sophie is beginning to wonder if she has made a unforgivable mistake.<br /><br />Because how well does she know Emma? Should she have trusted her to take care of her precious son?<br /><br />Sophie is about to discover the truth.And her life will never be the same.<br /><br /><br />It is absolutely terrifying when your child is gravely ill in hospital and you aren't with them,believe me I know from personal experience.So I could fully understand Sophie`s fear,guilt and desperate need to get to the hospital as quickly as possible.Trapped on a train with nothing else to do but panic and wait for updates on her son`s condition,Sophie takes us into the past and goes over the events leading up to her current situation.Through her eyes we meet the residents of the small village of Tedbury where she lives with her husband Mark and their young son Ben.Like most other small communities everyone knows everyone else's business and what they don't know,they make up.We get to see the inner workings of Sophie and Mark`s marriage,how and where she met Emma and the effect that seemingly innocent meeting had on her life and relashionships.There are parts that are voiced by other characters including Mark and Emma but the story is mainly voiced by our protagonist Sophie.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this well written,gripping thriller,it was intense,creepy and had a twist that I definitely didn't see coming.There where a few parts that where quite hard to read and I really felt a lot of sympathy for one character.This story really played with my emotions at times,a emotional roller coaster ride from the first page to the last.<br /><br /><br />Many thanks to Thomas &amp; Mercer for a arc of this book via Netgalley in exchange for a honest review.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2265606896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265606896" />
    <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley"><img alt="Liz Barnsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447272680p2/16471876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2265606896?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Barnsley" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley">Liz Barnsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781542046664" href="/book/show/35906811-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2265606896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12189434827983929458">Thoroughly enjoyed this one, it's had me banging through it ALL DAY. <br/><br/>So imagine that you are stuck on a train, miles from home, your child has been in an accident with his friend - the hospital don't know which is which - the injuries are severe perhaps more for one than the other - what do you do? Well there isn't a lot you CAN do except pray for the train to go faster and reflect on what has brought you here...<br/><br/>Therein lies the premise for "The Friend" - a twisty psychological thriller that fol</span>
  <span id="freeText12189434827983929458" style="display:none">Thoroughly enjoyed this one, it's had me banging through it ALL DAY. <br /><br />So imagine that you are stuck on a train, miles from home, your child has been in an accident with his friend - the hospital don't know which is which - the injuries are severe perhaps more for one than the other - what do you do? Well there isn't a lot you CAN do except pray for the train to go faster and reflect on what has brought you here...<br /><br />Therein lies the premise for "The Friend" - a twisty psychological thriller that follows Sophie's new friendship with Emma, a seemingly perfect pal, bringing a fresh new feel to the small village they live in, both with young children, they naturally gravitate together. Suddenly though divisions within this small community seem rife, gossip about Emma abounds and maybe she isn't quite as perfect as she seems...<br /><br />So things I loved about this: The position the author put her main protagonist in brought a fresh feel to the genre - you know how you often read these books and the idiotic actions of characters can make you crazy - there's danger lurking and they'll run right into it, usually having forgotten to charge their phones, or not bothering to call the police because of some unrelated thing they don't want to disclose, or you know all the plot ploys by now to make sure the reader has to wait for things to be revealed. In this case the main character has no option for stupidity, she's stuck on that damn train, so apart from some very natural hysterics, she has no options. As a reader this ensured I stayed right on her side. No rolling of eyes with this one...<br /><br />The story told in flashback as Sophie remembers it all, is clever and quite scary in places. We do see some things from other character's points of view but it's mostly Sophie who has had a fairly rough time of it, none of which I'll give away. Still, she is ripe for this new friendship, one that might be more toxic than even our external characters are beginning to realise...<br /><br />It was a page turner, to be sure. As we all wait for that darned train to get Sophie home, the story unfolding is fascinating and intriguing. The characters all have levels and I liked the exploration of friendship, real and otherwise, plus the family drama side was realistically described.<br /><br />Overall a really good read. Recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12189434827983929458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2225362148204550971" style="display:none"><br />Sophie is on the train when she receives a chilling call informing her that her son Ben and his friend were in an accident.               <span id="reviewTextContainer2523839218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7543774700954008757">My first book by Driscoll and it was a page-turner! The main character, Sophie, was so oblivious and naive though it was maddening. I don't know how someone can be around someone so much and not have any inclination that they aren't what they seem. This happens to my mother a lot, not this extreme but she does get taken in by quite a few people so I know it definitely happens to people on a regular basis. Sorry mom, but it is true. lol In my own opinion, you have to be either- 1) one of those pe</span>
  <span id="freeText7543774700954008757" style="display:none">My first book by Driscoll and it was a page-turner! The main character, Sophie, was so oblivious and naive though it was maddening. I don't know how someone can be around someone so much and not have any inclination that they aren't what they seem. This happens to my mother a lot, not this extreme but she does get taken in by quite a few people so I know it definitely happens to people on a regular basis. Sorry mom, but it is true. lol In my own opinion, you have to be either- 1) one of those people (and this is my mother) that just don't pay attention to the world around you, kind of like the people that don't notice their friends drive by on the road or will walk right by you in a store and never notice you in the aisle 2) you're narcissistic and so wrapped up in you and only you, all of the time and you just have no interest in other people and what they're doing or 3) your friend with the double life is so, extremely, good at living two lives and wearing two faces that there really is nothing in their personality or actions to garner suspicion when you're around them. <br /><br />And this is just my own two cents, so no one take it to heart. If it's happened to you or someone you know, for another reason that I didn't list, please feel free to enlighten me.</span>

<div id="review_2491366353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2491366353" />
    <a title="Bharath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12800930-bharath"><img alt="Bharath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523678858p2/12800930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2491366353?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bharath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bharath" href="/user/show/12800930-bharath">Bharath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35920727-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2491366353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6084259570947043981">This is a story which packs great pace, as good thrillers should. Sophie is on a train and distraught as her son Ben is one of two boys in hospital. Her husband Mark is on the train as well. <br/><br/>The story alternates between the present and the past. The story in the past starts off when Emma moves into town with her son Theo. Sophie likes her immediately and they get along very well. A shocking murder follows unnerving the local residents. While it seems an open and shut case initially, there is a h</span>
  <span id="freeText6084259570947043981" style="display:none">This is a story which packs great pace, as good thrillers should. Sophie is on a train and distraught as her son Ben is one of two boys in hospital. Her husband Mark is on the train as well. <br /><br />The story alternates between the present and the past. The story in the past starts off when Emma moves into town with her son Theo. Sophie likes her immediately and they get along very well. A shocking murder follows unnerving the local residents. While it seems an open and shut case initially, there is a hint that there may be more to it than meets the eye.<br /><br />As the story progresses, it is clear that Emma has a past which Sophie and others do not entirely know about. But does any of it matter today to her friend Sophie?<br /><br />There are some twists in the story, as one would expect towards the end. The book is a very easy and engrossing read, especially due to the fast pace and good characterization. And yet, the story in the later part of the book could have been much better.<br /><br />My rating: 3.75 / 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="6084259570947043981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2238023488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2238023488" />
    <a title="Eva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7281449-eva"><img alt="Eva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493833443p2/7281449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2238023488?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva" href="/user/show/7281449-eva">Eva</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35920727-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2238023488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3439958648701833108">Well, now. If, like me, you have trust issues sometimes and don't like meeting new people, let this story be a lesson!<br/><br/>Sophie is traveling on a train with her husband when she gets a phone call to say her four year old son, Ben, is in hospital. Sophie had left Ben in the care of her friend, Emma. She thought Emma could be trusted. They were kindred spirits after all. But how well does Sophie know Emma anyway? Was what happened to Ben truly an accident? Or is there something more sinister going on</span>
  <span id="freeText3439958648701833108" style="display:none">Well, now. If, like me, you have trust issues sometimes and don't like meeting new people, let this story be a lesson!<br /><br />Sophie is traveling on a train with her husband when she gets a phone call to say her four year old son, Ben, is in hospital. Sophie had left Ben in the care of her friend, Emma. She thought Emma could be trusted. They were kindred spirits after all. But how well does Sophie know Emma anyway? Was what happened to Ben truly an accident? Or is there something more sinister going on?<br /><br />The story of The Friend is mostly told through flashbacks from before Ben's accident. Emma and her son Theo move to a tiny village and Sophie quite quickly strikes up a friendship with her, despite the other village residents being rather wary of Emma. On top of that, the quiet village is rocked by a murder and slowly but surely, things are revealed that will make you never trust another living soul again.<br /><br />After having enjoyed I Am Watching You, I was very much looking forward to this new offering by Teresa Driscoll and I was not disappointed. There were a few things I didn't see coming and while I don't normally mention the ending, I must just say that this one blew me away. I didn't particularly like any of the characters although I did sympathise with Sophie throughout the story for various reasons. Not least of all, obviously being miles away and stuck on a train when you don't have the faintest idea what's happening to your child.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed The Friend. It held my attention from start to finish, even if it was maybe a tad slow in some places. A compelling tale that just goes to show you never really know someone and though sometimes the things you learn about other people can be mightily surprising, the one person who may just surprise you the most is yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3439958648701833108" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2319347328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319347328" />
    <a title="Vicki Willis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32195771-vicki-willis"><img alt="Vicki Willis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460316431p2/32195771.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319347328?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki Willis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki Willis" href="/user/show/32195771-vicki-willis">Vicki Willis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35920727-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32195771-vicki-willis?shelf=z-2019">z-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319347328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2425923055188713647">This is a psychological thriller that preys on every parent's nightmare - something happening to your child while you are far away. The book started with the now and went back to before to set up the story about what happened. There were twists and turns that I didn't see coming. The last 25% was full of tension and it had a satisfying ending. This is the second book I have read by this author and she is becoming a new favorite.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2511265354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511265354" />
    <a title="Stephanie ((Strazzybooks))" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4956641-stephanie-strazzybooks"><img alt="Stephanie ((Strazzybooks))" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598203036p2/4956641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511265354?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie ((Strazzybooks))" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie ((Strazzybooks))" href="/user/show/4956641-stephanie-strazzybooks">Stephanie ((Strazzybooks))</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35920727-the-friend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511265354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1478806521322579561">I really enjoyed Driscoll’s first novel I Am Watching You, but was disappointed by this one. <br/><br/><b> "But at the time there was no clue to the future – the consequences." </b><br/><br/>Emma and her young son Theo are new to a small UK village and Emma is super suspicious as a death rocks the village. She is the title “Friend” to Sophie, a dissatisfied housewife who lives in the village with her son Ben and husband. <br/>The whole novel focuses on who really is Emma? What happened in her past to make her so shady? Why did</span>
  <span id="freeText1478806521322579561" style="display:none">I really enjoyed Driscoll’s first novel I Am Watching You, but was disappointed by this one. <br /><br /><b> "But at the time there was no clue to the future – the consequences." </b><br /><br />Emma and her young son Theo are new to a small UK village and Emma is super suspicious as a death rocks the village. She is the title “Friend” to Sophie, a dissatisfied housewife who lives in the village with her son Ben and husband. <br />The whole novel focuses on who really is Emma? What happened in her past to make her so shady? Why did she come to this particular village? And how did it get to the point of both boys, Theo and Ben, ending up in the hospital (while Sophie desperately tries to get home on the train)?<br /><br />The story is told mostly in flashbacks, but the format felt too disjointed, and the same questions and information seemed to be repeated often. I just wanted to get to it already! <br />The reader keeps reading, hoping to piece together what happened, but as the novel went on I just found myself not caring at all. The suspense wasn’t there for me. The ‘twist’ at the end was extremely predictable and pretty disappointing in its cliche. The epilogue was just an info dump and a good example of ‘telling not showing’. <br /><br />I did like seeing more of the reoccurring characters of DI Sparks and private detective Matthew, from Driscoll’s first novel, though they only play a background role and sometimes felt randomly placed.<br /><br />Overall, this book felt like 5 different stories trying to be wrapped up into one neat package. It didn’t work for me, but perhaps others will find an intriguing story here. I will still check out Driscoll’s next novel, but I hope I enjoy it more than The Friend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1478806521322579561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HkPCg7LZ5DPSLo4CL/OKZKW4LI+oIMkXSONtFfOe0/AjcnL62C6irgNCYBl+tvVQCA9rjfFJKvvMqu3wwCqsVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q5XO1EPNHuTbFpjcHGJtVJkFqDxBlheOJuW5BSCbzeGWpH6tKTpYeQp6dsdNJxJgNLLvPhj/9GKirDngEy+yRw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7970305.Teresa_Driscoll">About Teresa Driscoll</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7970305.Teresa_Driscoll"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1427445391p3/7970305.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7970305.Teresa_Driscoll">Teresa Driscoll
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,651
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15720946024497853789">Teresa Driscoll - a former BBC TV news presenter- is now an international #1 bestselling author. Her debut psychological suspense I AM WATCHING YOU hit Number One on Kindle in the UK, USA and Australia and sold more than half a million copies in its first year. Her second thriller THE FRIEND was also Kindle #1 in the UK and Australia and a top #10 bestseller in the USA. <br/>Teresa also writes women's </span>
  <span id="freeText15720946024497853789" style="display:none">Teresa Driscoll - a former BBC TV news presenter- is now an international #1 bestselling author. Her debut psychological suspense I AM WATCHING YOU hit Number One on Kindle in the UK, USA and Australia and sold more than half a million copies in its first year. Her second thriller THE FRIEND was also Kindle #1 in the UK and Australia and a top #10 bestseller in the USA. <br />Teresa also writes women's fiction. Her debut in this genre RECIPES FOR MELISSA was auctioned at the Frankfurt book fair between seven German publishers and her second women's fiction title is LAST KISS GOODNIGHT.<br />During her long career as a journalist, Teresa worked for newspapers, magazines and television, including 15 years presenting the BBC TV news programme Spotlight. Covering crime for so long, she was deeply moved by the haunting impact on the relatives, the friends and the witnesses and it is those ripples she explores now in her darker fiction.<br />Teresa's books have been sold for translation in 15 languages. She lives in glorious Devon with her husband and two sons and blogs regularly about her "writing life" at her website - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.teresadriscoll.com">www.teresadriscoll.com</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15720946024497853789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
